<rate>5< /rate>< Text>
There's a lot of activity and facilities for the residents of that's community that the residents have no reason to stay inside and sit on a couch to watch TV the when day. Dance lessons, tennis, swimming, pickle ball, ping pong are just some of the things in the program. The ping pong hall located at the Thurs floor of the community center is awesome, huge and well lighted with about 30 tables. The centerpiece is the 3 nine-hole golf course, well-maintained fairways and greens. There are no water hazards but the bunkers are well placed. Lengthwise, it is fair and set up is challenging. This is a great community and a great place to retire.</Text>

< text>
We have lived here now for 3 years. This place was the cheapest in OC to purchase a ok place. It has changed for the worse during these 3 years. The board is doing all they can to make it difficult to sell your place. The administrative fee when you purchase a place went from $2.500 to $5.000. Laguna woods village is a very FEE HAPPY place. There is fees for pretty much EVERYTHING.......and yes the HOA FEE is $652 and will go up again this year. Like someone said they are trying to make this in to a 5 star resort - that will most likely not occur, but in the mean time they sure are trying. When we retire we will move, can NOT afford to reside here. It almost seems like there is more rentals than owners living here. Also lot of mean ladies living here, when you walk your dog they can very well come out from their 'cave' and be nasty. Chose carefully which gate you want to live in.<//text>

< userid>
106289270782979631381</userid>
<user_name>Kath leen< /user_name><Time>1429667101596</Time><Rating>5< /Rating>< review>
Customize your fries! Best thing ever!
I wish the franchise would open up a few locations in Bay Area!

First - You get to choose a type of fries you want. Such as regular fries, curly fries and sweet potato fries. Sweet potato fries are the best!

Second - Pick a flavor! Cheddar, Chili BBQ, BBQ, Sour Cream and Garlic Parm. My two favorites are cheddar and chili BBQ. The cheddar is pretty much plain and simple while the chili BBQ has quite a kick!

Third - Pick a size! Jumbo (small), Mega (medium), Giga (large)

The guy at the register was super friendly, nice and suggested good recommendations. Sadly, they ran out sour cream and garlic parm, the two flavors that I really wanted to try. However, the customer service from the guy was great, so I settled for cheddar.

This snack is easy to eat on the go and definitely not health friendly. If I lived in SoCal, I'll probably be grubbing on Potato Corner weekly!

Potato Corner is special because you literally can customize to your heart's content!<//review>

<Name>Sandi Medina< /Name>< review>
My sister took my mom to process my brother's passport on 12/11/18. The woman had the worst attitude, when my mom asked for help with the application after something was wrong on it, she annoyingly said she could not help. She was not friendly at all. They had to go back a second time, it was the first time she processed a passport here in the U.S. and the worker expected her to know all the fees. They had to go get a money order since apparently they don't take cash there and when they got back they needed another money order for the processing fee and picture which wasn't mentioned the first time. Pricing signs would help and a no cash sign too. Very disappointed. Will not be returning. Some people need training on better customer service. I processed my own in Santa Barbara and it was great loved the friendly environment helpfulness.< /review>

Daiso is a great store in the Peace Plaza shopping center, in the Japantown neighborhood of San Francisco. It is a chain store but I have only been to this location.

< review>
Wonderful daiso, and quite large in comparison to other locations I have visited in northern California. Very clean, spacious and easy to keep 6ft away while perusing the long aisles. Store was very neat and tidy, cleaning witnessed in multiple areas during my visit. A lot of items that were a surprise to me on the shelf as I would have needed to travel to 2 or even 3 different daiso locations to find all the items. Stationery and crafts were large full aisles and a lot of options presented (what I normally check out). Staff was quick to help me find items and checkout was very efficient. Definitely visit any time I am in the downtown area.< /review>

This place rocks! It's worth going to this one as opposed to the smaller one on 16th St Plaza. Great place to buy coin batteries - great selection. Just be aware that you can't return anything. <user_name>drawonnoodles<//user_name>< text>
COVID-19 review: The last time for entry is 6:40pm even though the business closes at 7pm so be mindful. There is a line outside now and closed off the previous main entrance inside. I went on a Wednesday afternoon and there wasnt too much of a line. They do let very few people in though, lot less than other stores so the wait may be a little long. There was lots of room to socially distance so I felt very comfortable shopping. This Daiso was a lot better years ago with a lot more inventory. They've downsized for a while now but I guess that's business. Items also got more expensive. They do have a lot of really useful household items for cheap -- things you didnt know you wanted. Of course, don't come here for quality items but if you want quick fixes this is the place to go.

Pre-COVID: The place was always overly crowded and stuffy. You smell people's breath in the stuffiness. A bit stingy on the A/C? Sometimes the line would get so long you have to wait a good 30-40minutes. Totally not worth.< /text>

<pictures>None< /pictures><text>Think of your local $1 store.  Daiso is the $1.50 store Japanese store with some real quality items with something for just about everyone.  Unless noted, all items are $1.50.  I've never seen an item for more than $3.00 in there.

Items I look for whenever I visit Daiso: Travel accessories, travel wipes, house slippers, pens, stationary, notebooks, cards, organizing containers, Japanese snacks and soft drinks.   They have $1.50 Japanese items for every room in the house. The products they offer are exclusive to Daiso stores only which enhances the visit.  It's easy to get carried away in here because the items are so cheap but after years of visits I've narrowed downs my list. hehe  Like the $1 stores, products come and go so timing is everything in regards to finding things I'm looking for.  Overall, I've never walked out of there with a light bag.

Located in Japan town, this Daiso store always enhances my visit there.
The value I've encountered through the years shopping as been fantastic.  Whenever I anticipate a Daiso visit, I'll pack a larger luggage just in case I go to town in there.  Swing by and browse around if you have to be in the area.  Good Luck!</text>< username>
Steff A.< /username>

< Text>
One of the larger Daiso in San Francisco. Compared to the Daiso at the Serramonte shopping center, this has just as much merchandise and selection despite being smaller. Wide selection of ceramics and Asian amenities that don't just come and go. I bought a good quality calligraphy stone a few years ago and they continue to carry it. From school supplies to basic hardware tools. Hardware tools are very low quality so don't expect much unless you're in a pinch.< /Text>

It's not bad for $1.50 store, they have tupperware, kitchen supplies, claypots (big and small), food, etc. The rule is pretty simple too: everything is $1.50 unless a price is listed.  So if no price tag, then it's $1.50.  I had to buy an iphone cord since mine was breaking.  bought one here for $1.50 and it works great like any other cord would.</Review>

<review>I love Daiso. Pleasantly surprised to find this one in J-Town. Considering its location, I thought it was pretty large! Although not as large as my favorite location in Union City.

Great spot to pick up stocking stuffers or just things you didn't know you needed. Everything for the most part costs $1.50. Last trip I scored:

* Calpico drink - Called "Calpis" in Japan, my daughter refused to drink it because she thought it was cow pee. But it's really a tasty milk-based drink.
* Mittens - Cute red ones with smiling bunnies.
* Notebooks - Tons and tons of 'em.
* Mini plastic containers - Made in Japan (unlike a lot of the stuff here made in China for Daiso), these are so handy for lunches, thumbtacks, vitamins, whatever.
* Office supplies - staplers, paper clips, pens, etc.
* Cute tape - In skinny or wider versions, this is printed colorful tape that is great for wrapping gifts or just being funny. Last one I got said, "Celabrate the day of you birth."

I dare you to come in here and walk away empty handed.< /review><Response>None<//Response></record>
</dataset><record>
<pictures>None<//pictures><GmapID>0x808580bec47c4937:0xce6cc26aae769b00< /GmapID>< Text>
I feel like there's always something I can buy for $1.50 here that I could use whether it's a notebook, a shower cap or a Santa Claus costume ($5). A few things are more than $1.50 but that's ok--it's still insanely cheap.  They have a good selection of wrapping paper and gift wrapping ideas at this location.  I like looking at all the cute bakeware and bento lunch making ware they have here.  Service was great this time I went because, I had a lot of coins I wanted to get rid of.  She said I could go ahead and throw all the coins on the table.  She calculated it all and lightened my coin purse. Domo agigato girl at Daiso!</Text>
